<pictures>None<//pictures>< Text>
This gym works for me.  I find the staff quite nice and helpful, the trainers I used were first-rate (sometimes that's luck of the draw) and the equipment varied and well maintained.  My schedule permits midday visits when the gym isn't crowded, so that's an added plus.  I've heard that evenings are packed but that's probably true for any gym.

If you're looking for a place with a pool, sauna and babysitters, this isn't for you.  However, they do have good classes which you get with a $20/month membership.  If classes aren't your interest, the basic gym price is around $10/month.  Hard to beat.

Oh, by the way, Angel and George are there everyday so not sure what the other reviewer is talking about.<//Text>

<userid>113372890584324777750< /userid><user_name>Nacho Cheese<//user_name><Date>1461647850892</Date><rating>4<//rating>< Review>
This gym is for anyone on a budget. I have been going to this gym for about a year now. I will give you an idea of what it is to go to this Crunch Gym.

Pros: Very Cheap. Who can't afford $10 a month.(Basis) Even $20 (Peak) a month? The atmosphere in the building is quite positive. Everyone is there to make them selves physically better.  I have not felt uncomfortable working out. Another pro is that the bathrooms and lockers are always clean.

Cons: It gets very busy around night time. Around 7- Closing time it is the worst time to go. That is when everyone is off work. The customer service evens itself out. You have the nice employees that are very professional and then you have some that look like they don't want to be there.

Tips if you do end up signing up to this gym.
*The best times to go to this particular gym is to go in the morning if you can. If you work evening shifts then you will have the gym to yourself. If you work mornings then it would be best to do use some workout machines that are mostly taken. For example I would workout your chest or legs on the weekends to be able to use the squat rack or the bench press benches. Most of the times not a lot of people go to the gym on the weekends.
* If they ask you to pay $100 for the starting fee. Please don't. Make sure you find a flier that says $0 dollars enrollment fee. Or find it on their website that proves that they can lower or by any ads that show up.  Trust me they can bring it down.

In all it's a good gym if you are in a budget. Would recommend a friend to join.< /Review>

<text>I've dined in at Galanga in the past as well as have ordered to go, and tonight I put an order in for delivery. Not once have I been disappointed with their food. Usually I play it safe by ordering the Galanga fried rice with chicken which is good! However, tonight I wanted to try something different from the menu. <Text>Galanga
Thai fusion
This small restaurant on Santa Monica avenue in west Hollywood is a great place for a quick lunch If you are there by chance, or because you work or live in the neighborhood; you will not get disappointed. There are tables inside and also in the little sunny garden in the back.
Their curries are the best; yellow, green or red,  with fish, chicken or shrimp, (at your taste or tolerance )from mild to spicy hot. It comes with vegetables and rice, delicious flavors of coconut cream, spices and ginger of the Thai cuisine.
Salads, seafood, fish and duck dishes are also a good choice from the menu a la carte.
Prices are reasonable, for a two course lunch and tea or soda probably you will pay around 15 dollars.
Don‚Äôt expect much from the service or the ambience, but you will get a nice smile, politeness from the owners and a flavorful, honest fresh meal.</Text>< resp>

<Rate>5<//Rate><Text>Perfectly tasty Thai dishes! Their appetizer (sampler for two) is a great way to get a taste of some items before your entree. It has mainly fried items and a fresh spring roll to share.

I always try the curry but this time I got the vegetable curry for $8.95. The price was fantastic and so was the meal. It's my new favorite dish here. I tried Panang, yellow, and the red curry here before- all just as delicious and highly recommended depending on what veggies you would prefer in the curry. This one said it had asparagus but it had zucchini instead.

Parking is in the street and some in the side I believe but you're better off getting street parking and usually from the four times I've been here so far- there has been no problems getting parking. Right out front too.

Atmosphere is really laid back and casual. There's indoor seating and outdoor seating in the back. I've never had to wait but I wouldn't be surprised on a weekend if this place fills up.

Highly suggest this place, it's fresh, authenticand prices are great.< /Text>< pics>

We use to go to a different Thai resturant off of Hollywood Blvd but we wanted to try a different place. The reviews looked pretty good so we went here around 2 pm on a Thursday so there wasn't really a lot of people. The parking situation wasn't the best but it wasn't terrible. We got seated quickly and and got our drinks, a Thai tea and a Thai coffee. They were both amazing! Not to sweet but not to bitter. We ordered just normal pho and a pad Thai and damn were they flavorful and amazing. I can't really explain the taste but it was the best I've ever had. The portions were large and everything was cheap. We will be coming back when we visit again.< /text>

<Text>I ordered a new MacBook Pro ($2,400) set to ship to my home. I was alerted that the package was redirected to the FedEx at Walgreens on Otis. We did not initiate the redirect and confirmed that Apple didn't either.  When I went to pick it up, they couldn't find it. My FedEx tracking information said it had been signed for with my first initial and last name just a couple hours before I arrived. The acting manager went back to look at the security footage and saw a guy come in at the time it was signed for and he took the package. He showed me a photo of the footage it showed that the Walgreens employee at the time looked at an ID from the guy and then handed him the package.

They questioned the employee and she said his ID said my exact name and that she doesn't know the guy (of course, they have to take her word as the security footage can't make out the text on an ID). I don't buy it. The odds of that guy knowing to walk into that store and ask to pick up a MacBook package with my exact name on it at that exact time is impossible to be a coincidence. And even if there were two people with my exact name that both happened to order MacBooks that happened to each be sitting at that location at the same time, there would have been another one when I went in.

We believe she is calling a friend when a high value package shows up in their (unbelievably disheveled) holding area, gives him the name on the package to say when he comes in, then as long as he presents any ID, it appears on security footage that she did her job. Then he walks out and they split the sale of the stolen goods later. That part of the scam feels fairly clear.

The part that's a bit odd is why FedEx rerouted my package when neither the sender (Apple) nor recipient (me) initiated it. Note: we asked for details of the redirect origin and they would only release the last 4 digits of the phone number, which we of course didn't recognize. We wonder whether someone working at FedEx is also in on the operation who has both visibility into packages coming to the local area and the authority to redirect them to that location. They'd be very familiar with the labeling from well-known brand shipments like Apple and could easily call up the gal at Walgreens (presumably a friend) and coordinate the delivery time around her shift schedule.

Note: the manager has all my information and still has not contacted me once, though I've emailed several times with the guy I dealt with at the store and he keeps telling me the manager will reach out.< /Text>< Response>
